963 <section id="_1">

964

965 <h2>

966General Information About Salivary Gland Cancer</h2>

967

968 <div id="_section_1" class="pdq-sections">

969<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

970<h6>

971In This Section</h6>

972<ul>

973<li>

976</li>

980</li>

1003</li>

1004<li>

1009</a>

1011</ul>

1012</nav>

1013<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

1014<a href="/types/head-and-neck/patient/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq">

1015Go to Patient Version</a>

1016</div>

1017<section id="_403">

1018<h3 id="_403_toc">

1019Incidence and Mortality</h3>

1020<p id="_123" tabindex="-1">

1021Salivary gland tumors are a morphologically and clinically diverse group of neoplasms, which may present significant diagnostic and management challenges. These tumors are rare, with an overall incidence in the Western world of approximately 2.5 to 3.0 cases per 100,000 people per year.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

10221</a>

1023] Malignant salivary gland neoplasms account for more than 0.5% of all malignancies and approximately 3% to 5% of all head and neck cancers.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

10241</a>

1025,<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

10262</a>

1027] Most patients with malignant salivary gland tumors are in their sixth or seventh decade of life.[<a href="#cit/section_1.3">

10283</a>

1029,<a href="#cit/section_1.4">

10304</a>

1031] </p>

1032</section>

1033<section id="_404">

1034<h3 id="_404_toc">

1035Carcinogenesis and Risk Factors</h3>

1036<p id="_405" tabindex="-1">

1037Although exposure to ionizing radiation has been implicated as a cause of salivary gland cancer, the etiology of most salivary gland cancers cannot be determined.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

10382</a>

1039,<a href="#cit/section_1.3">

10403</a>

1041,<a href="#cit/section_1.5">

10425</a>

1043,<a href="#cit/section_1.6">

10446</a>

1045] Occupations associated with an increased risk for salivary gland cancers include rubber products manufacturing, asbestos mining, plumbing, and some types of woodworking.[<a href="#cit/section_1.3">

10463</a>

1047]</p>

1048</section>

1049<section id="_406">

1050<h3 id="_406_toc">

1051Anatomy</h3>

1052<p id="_3" tabindex="-1">

1053Tumors of the salivary glands comprise those in the major glands (e.g., parotid,

1054submandibular, and sublingual) and the minor glands (e.g., oral mucosa, palate, uvula,

1055floor of mouth, posterior tongue, retromolar area and peritonsillar area,

1056pharynx, larynx, and paranasal sinuses).[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

10572</a>

1058,<a href="#cit/section_1.7">

10597</a>

1060] Minor salivary gland lesions are most frequently seen in the oral cavity.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

10612</a>

1062]

1063</p>

1064<p id="_419" tabindex="-1">

1065Of salivary gland neoplasms, more than 50% are benign, and approximately 70% to 80% originate in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

10661</a>

1067,<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

10682</a>

1069,<a href="#cit/section_1.8">

10708</a>

1071] The palate is the most common site of minor salivary gland tumors. The frequency of malignant lesions varies by site. Approximately 20% to 25% of parotid tumors, 35% to 40% of submandibular tumors, 50% of palate tumors, and more than 90% of sublingual gland tumors are malignant.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

10721</a>

1073,<a href="#cit/section_1.9">

10749</a>

1075]</p>

1076</section>

1077<section id="_408">

1078<h3 id="_408_toc">

1079Histopathology</h3>

1080<p id="_125" tabindex="-1">

1081Histologically, salivary gland tumors represent the most heterogenous group of tumors of any tissue in the body.[<a href="#cit/section_1.10">

108210</a>

1083] Although almost 40 histological types of epithelial tumors of the salivary glands exist, some are exceedingly rare and may be the subject of only a few case reports.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

10841</a>

1085,<a href="#cit/section_1.11">

108611</a>

1087] The most common benign major and minor salivary gland tumor is pleomorphic adenoma, which makes up about 50% of all salivary gland tumors and 65% of parotid gland tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

10881</a>

1089] The most common malignant major and minor salivary gland tumor is mucoepidermoid carcinoma, which represents about 10% of all salivary gland neoplasms and approximately 35% of malignant salivary gland neoplasms.[<a href="#cit/section_1.1">

10901</a>

1091,<a href="#cit/section_1.12">

109212</a>

1093] This neoplasm occurs most often in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

10942</a>

1095,<a href="#cit/section_1.12">

109612</a>

1097,<a href="#cit/section_1.13">

109813</a>

1099] For more information about this type and other histological types of salivary gland neoplasms, see the <a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_6">

1100Cellular Classification of Salivary Gland Cancer</a>

1101 section.</p>

1102</section>

1103<section id="_409">

1104<h3 id="_409_toc">

1105Clinical Presentation</h3>

1106<p id="_126" tabindex="-1">

1107Most patients with benign tumors of the major or minor salivary glands present with painless swelling of the parotid, submandibular, or sublingual glands. Neurological signs, such as numbness or weakness caused by nerve involvement, typically indicate a malignancy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

11082</a>

1109] Facial nerve weakness associated with a parotid or submandibular tumor is an ominous sign. Persistent facial pain is highly suggestive of malignancy. Approximately 10% to 15% of malignant parotid neoplasms present with pain.[<a href="#cit/section_1.8">

11108</a>

1111,<a href="#cit/section_1.14">

111214</a>

1113] However, most parotid tumors, both benign and malignant, present as an asymptomatic mass in the gland.[<a href="#cit/section_1.2">

11142</a>

1115,<a href="#cit/section_1.8">

11168</a>

1117] For more information, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/pain/pain-hp-pdq">

1118Cancer Pain</a>

1119. </p>

1120</section>

1121<section id="_410">

1122<h3 id="_410_toc">

1123Prognostic Factors</h3>

1124<p id="_4" tabindex="-1">

1125Early-stage, low-grade, malignant salivary gland tumors are usually curable by adequate

1126surgical resection alone. The prognosis is more favorable when the tumor is

1127in a major salivary gland. The parotid gland is most favorable followed by the submandibular gland. The least favorable primary sites are the sublingual and minor salivary glands. Large bulky tumors or high-grade tumors carry a poorer

1128prognosis and may best be treated by surgical resection combined with

1129postoperative radiation therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.15">

113015</a>

1131] The prognosis also depends on the following factors:[<a href="#cit/section_1.16">

113216</a>

1133,<a href="#cit/section_1.17">

113417</a>

1135]

1136

1137</p>

1138<div class="pdq-content-list">

1139<ul id="_211">

1140<li>

1141 Gland in which

1142they arise.</li>

1143<li>

1144Histology.</li>

1145<li>

1146Grade (i.e., degree of malignancy).</li>

1147<li>

1148Extent of primary tumor

1149(i.e., the stage).</li>

1150<li>

1151Whether the tumor involves the facial nerve, has fixation to the

1152skin or deep structures, or has spread to lymph nodes or distant sites.</li>

1153</ul>

1154</div>

1155</section>

1156<section id="_411">

1157<h3 id="_411_toc">

1158Follow-Up and Survivorship</h3>

1159<p id="_212" tabindex="-1">

1160 Overall, clinical stage, particularly tumor size, may be the crucial factor to determine the outcome of salivary gland cancer and may be more important than histological grade.[<a href="#cit/section_1.18">

116118</a>

1162]</p>

1163<section id="_412">

1164<h4 id="_412_toc">

1165Treatment management</h4>

1166<p id="_127" tabindex="-1">

1167Perineural invasion can also occur, particularly in high-grade adenoid

1168cystic carcinoma, and should be specifically identified and treated.[<a href="#cit/section_1.19">

116919</a>

1170]

1171Radiation therapy may increase the chance of local control and increase the survival of patients

1172when adequate margins cannot be achieved.[<a href="#cit/section_1.20">

117320</a>

1174][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

1175Level of evidence C2</a>

1176]

1177Unresectable or recurrent tumors may respond to chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_1.21">

117821</a>

1179-<a href="#cit/section_1.23">

118023</a>

1181] Fast

1182neutron-beam radiation therapy or accelerated hyperfractionated photon-beam

1183schedules have been effective in the treatment of inoperable,

1184unresectable, and recurrent tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_1.24">

118524</a>

1186-<a href="#cit/section_1.26">

118726</a>

1188]</p>

1189</section>

1190<section id="_413">

1191<h4 id="_413_toc">

1192Follow-up after treatment</h4>

1193<p id="_128" tabindex="-1">

1194Complications of surgical treatment for parotid neoplasms include facial nerve dysfunction and Frey syndrome (also known as gustatory flushing and sweating and auriculotemporal syndrome).[<a href="#cit/section_1.8">

11958</a>

1196] Frey syndrome has been successfully treated with injections of botulinum toxin A.[<a href="#cit/section_1.27">

119727</a>

1198-<a href="#cit/section_1.29">

119929</a>

1200]</p>

1320

1321 <section id="_6">

1322

1323 <h2>

1324Cellular Classification of Salivary Gland Cancer</h2>

1325

1326 <div id="_section_6" class="pdq-sections">

1327<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

1328<h6>

1329In This Section</h6>

1330<ul>

1331<li>

1332<a href="#_132_toc">

1333Epithelial Neoplasms</a>

1334</li>

1335<li>

1336<a href="#_192_toc">

1337Nonepithelial Neoplasms</a>

1338</li>

1339<li>

1340<a href="#_200_toc">

1341Malignant Secondary Neoplasms</a>

1342</li>

1343</ul>

1344</nav>

1345<p id="_129" tabindex="-1">

1346Salivary gland neoplasms are remarkable for their histological diversity. These neoplasms include benign and malignant tumors of epithelial, mesenchymal, and lymphoid origin. Salivary gland tumors pose a particular challenge to the surgical pathologist. Differentiating benign from malignant tumors may be difficult, primarily because of the complexity of the classification and the rarity of several entities, which may exhibit a broad spectrum of morphological diversity in individual lesions.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

13471</a>

1348] In some cases, hybrid lesions may be seen.[<a href="#cit/section_2.2">

13492</a>

1350] The key guiding principle to establish the malignant nature of a salivary gland tumor is the demonstration of an infiltrative margin.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

13511</a>

1352] </p>

1353<p id="_130" tabindex="-1">

1354The following cellular classification scheme draws heavily from a scheme published by the Armed Forces Institute of Pathology (AFIP).[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

13553</a>

1356] Malignant nonepithelial neoplasms are included in the scheme because these neoplasms comprise a significant proportion of salivary gland neoplasms seen in the clinical setting. For completeness, malignant secondary tumors are also included in the scheme.</p>

1357<p id="_131" tabindex="-1">

1358Where AFIP statistics regarding the incidence, or relative frequency, of particular histopathologies are cited, some bias may exist because of the AFIP methods of case accrual as a pathology reference service. When possible, other sources are cited for incidence data. Notwithstanding the AFIP data, the incidence of a particular histopathology has been found to vary considerably depending upon the study cited. This variability in reporting may be partially caused by the rare incidence of many salivary gland neoplasms.</p>

1359<section id="_132">

1360<h3 id="_132_toc">

1361Epithelial Neoplasms</h3>

1362<p id="_133" tabindex="-1">

1363The clinician should be aware that several benign epithelial salivary gland neoplasms have malignant counterparts, which are discussed below:[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

13643</a>

1365]</p>

1366<div class="pdq-content-list">

1367<ul id="_134">

1368<li>

1369Pleomorphic adenoma (i.e., mixed tumor). For more information, see the <a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_301">

1370Carcinoma ex pleomorphic adenoma</a>

1371 section.</li>

1372<li>

1373 Warthin tumor, also known as papillary cystadenoma lymphomatosum.</li>

1374<li>

1375 Monomorphic adenomas:<div class="pdq-content-list">

1376<ul id="_135" class="list-dash">

1377<li>

1378Basal cell adenoma. For more information, see the <a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_381">

1379Basal cell adenocarcinoma</a>

1380 section.</li>

1381<li>

1382 Canalicular adenoma. </li>

1383<li>

1384 Oncocytoma. For more information, see the <a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_386">

1385Oncocytic carcinoma</a>

1386 section.</li>

1387<li>

1388 Sebaceous adenoma. </li>

1389<li>

1390 Sebaceous lymphadenoma. For more information, see the <a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_385">

1391Sebaceous lymphadenocarcinoma</a>

1392 section.</li>

1393</ul>

1394</div>

1395</li>

1396<li>

1397 Myoepithelioma. For more information, see the <a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_311">

1398Myoepithelial carcinoma</a>

1399 section.</li>

1400<li>

1401 Cystadenoma. For more information, see the <a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_383">

1402Cystadenocarcinoma</a>

1403 section.</li>

1404<li>

1405 Ductal papillomas.</li>

1406<li>

1407 Sialoblastoma.</li>

1408</ul>

1409</div>

1410<p id="_136" tabindex="-1">

1411Histological grading of salivary gland carcinomas is important to determine the proper treatment approach, although it is not an independent indicator of the clinical course and must be considered in the context of the clinical stage. Clinical stage, particularly tumor size, may be the critical factor to determine the outcome of salivary gland cancer and may be more important than histological grade.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

14121</a>

1413] For example, stage I intermediate-grade or high-grade mucoepidermoid carcinomas can be successfully treated, whereas low-grade mucoepidermoid carcinomas that present as stage III disease may have a very aggressive clinical course.[<a href="#cit/section_2.4">

14144</a>

1415]</p>

1416<p id="_137" tabindex="-1">

1417Grading is used primarily for mucoepidermoid carcinomas, adenocarcinomas, not otherwise specified (NOS), adenoid cystic carcinomas, and squamous cell carcinomas.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

14181</a>

1419,<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

14203</a>

1421] Various other salivary gland carcinomas can also be categorized according to histological grade as follows:[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

14223</a>

1423,<a href="#cit/section_2.5">

14245</a>

1425-<a href="#cit/section_2.8">

14268</a>

1427]</p>

1428<p id="_138" tabindex="-1">

1429<strong>

1430Low grade</strong>

1431</p>

1432<div class="pdq-content-list">

1433<ul id="_139">

1434<li>

1435<a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_291">

1436Acinic cell carcinoma</a>

1673<section id="_218">

1674<h5 id="_218_toc">

1675Mucoepidermoid carcinoma</h5>

1676<p id="_219" tabindex="-1">

1677Mucoepidermoid carcinoma is a malignant epithelial tumor that is composed of various proportions of mucous, epidermoid (e.g., squamous), intermediate, columnar, and clear cells and often demonstrates prominent cystic growth. It is the most common malignant neoplasm observed in the major and minor salivary glands.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

16781</a>

1679,<a href="#cit/section_2.9">

16809</a>

1681] Mucoepidermoid carcinoma represents 29% to 34% of malignant tumors originating in both major and minor salivary glands.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

16823</a>

1683,<a href="#cit/section_2.5">

16845</a>

1685,<a href="#cit/section_2.10">

168610</a>

1687,<a href="#cit/section_2.11">

168811</a>

1689] In two large retrospective series, 84% to 93% of cases originated in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.12">

169012</a>

1691,<a href="#cit/section_2.13">

169213</a>

1693] With regard to malignant tumors of the minor salivary glands, mucoepidermoid carcinoma shows a strong predilection for the lower lip.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

16943</a>

1695,<a href="#cit/section_2.14">

169614</a>

1697] In an AFIP review of civilian cases, the mean age of patients was 47 years (range, 8&#8211;92 years).[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

16983</a>

1699] Prior exposure to ionizing radiation appears to substantially increase the risk of developing malignant neoplasms of the major salivary glands, particularly mucoepidermoid carcinoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

17003</a>

1701,<a href="#cit/section_2.13">

170213</a>

1703]</p>

1704<p id="_220" tabindex="-1">

1705Most patients are asymptomatic and present with solitary, painless masses. Symptoms include pain, drainage from the ipsilateral ear, dysphagia, trismus, and facial paralysis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

17063</a>

1707] For more information, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/pain/pain-hp-pdq">

1708Cancer Pain</a>

1709.</p>

1710<p id="_221" tabindex="-1">

1711Microscopic grading of mucoepidermoid carcinoma is important to determine the prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

17121</a>

1713,<a href="#cit/section_2.12">

171412</a>

1715,<a href="#cit/section_2.15">

171615</a>

1717] Mucoepidermoid carcinomas are graded as low grade, intermediate grade, and high grade. Grading parameters with point values include the following:</p>

1718<div class="pdq-content-list">

1719<ul id="_222">

1720<li>

1721Intracystic

1722component (+2).</li>

1723<li>

1724Neural invasion present (+2).</li>

1725<li>

1726Necrosis present (+3).</li>

1727<li>

1728Mitosis (&#8805;4 per 10 high-power field [+3]).</li>

1729<li>

1730Anaplasia present (+4).</li>

1731</ul>

1732</div>

1733<p id="_223" tabindex="-1">

1734Total point scores are 0 to 4 for low grade, 5 to 6 for intermediate grade, and 7 to 14 for high grade.</p>

1735<p id="_224" tabindex="-1">

1736In a retrospective review of 243 cases of mucoepidermoid carcinoma of the major salivary glands, a statistically significant correlation was shown between this point-based grading system and outcome for parotid tumors but not for submandibular tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_2.12">

173712</a>

1738] Another retrospective study that used this histological grading system indicated that tumor grade correlated well with prognosis for mucoepidermoid carcinoma of the major salivary glands, excluding submandibular tumors, and minor salivary glands.[<a href="#cit/section_2.13">

173913</a>

1740] A modification of this grading system placed more emphasis on features of tumor invasion.[<a href="#cit/section_2.16">

174116</a>

1742] Nonetheless, though tumor grade may be useful, stage appears to be a better indicator of prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

17433</a>

1744,<a href="#cit/section_2.16">

174516</a>

1746]</p>

1747<p id="_225" tabindex="-1">

1748Cytogenetically, mucoepidermoid carcinoma is characterized by a t(11;19)(q14&#8211;21;p12&#8211;13) translocation, which is occasionally the sole cytogenetic alteration.[<a href="#cit/section_2.17">

174917</a>

1750-<a href="#cit/section_2.19">

175119</a>

1752] This translocation creates a novel fusion product, <em class="gene-name">

1753MECT1</em>

1754::<em class="gene-name">

1755MAML2</em>

1756, which disrupts a Notch signaling pathway.[<a href="#cit/section_2.20">

175720</a>

1758] Notch signaling plays a key role in the normal development of many tissues and cell types, through diverse effects on cellular differentiation, survival, and/or proliferation, and may be involved in a wide variety of human neoplasms.[<a href="#cit/section_2.21">

175921</a>

1760]</p>

1761<p id="_226" tabindex="-1">

1762Rarely, mucoepidermoid carcinoma may originate within the jaws. This tumor type is known as central mucoepidermoid carcinoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

17633</a>

1764] The mandibular to maxillary predilection is approximately 3:1.[<a href="#cit/section_2.22">

176522</a>

1766] </p>

1767</section>

1768<section id="_227">

1769<h5 id="_227_toc">

1770Adenoid cystic carcinoma</h5>

1771<p id="_228" tabindex="-1">

1772Adenoid cystic carcinoma, formerly known as cylindroma, is a slow growing but aggressive neoplasm with a remarkable capacity for recurrence.[<a href="#cit/section_2.23">

177323</a>

1774] Morphologically, three growth patterns have been described: cribriform, or classic pattern; tubular; and solid, or basaloid pattern. The tumors are categorized according to the predominant pattern.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

17753</a>

1776,<a href="#cit/section_2.23">

177723</a>

1778-<a href="#cit/section_2.25">

177925</a>

1780] The cribriform pattern shows epithelial cell nests that form cylindrical patterns. The lumina of these spaces contain periodic acid-Schiff (PAS)-positive mucopolysaccharide secretions. The tubular pattern reveals tubular structures that are lined by stratified cuboidal epithelium. The solid pattern shows solid groups of cuboidal cells. The cribriform pattern is the most common, and the solid pattern is the least common.[<a href="#cit/section_2.26">

178126</a>

1782] Solid adenoid cystic carcinoma is a high-grade lesion with reported recurrence rates of as much as 100%, compared with 50% to 80% for the tubular and cribriform variants.[<a href="#cit/section_2.25">

178325</a>

1784]</p>

1785<p id="_229" tabindex="-1">

1786In a review of its case files, the AFIP found adenoid cystic carcinoma to be the fifth most common malignant epithelial tumor of the salivary glands after mucoepidermoid carcinomas; adenocarcinomas, NOS; acinic cell carcinomas; and PLGA.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

17873</a>

1788] Other series, however, reported adenoid cystic carcinoma to be the second most common malignant tumor, with an incidence or relative frequency of approximately 20%.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

17891</a>

1790] In the AFIP data, this neoplasm constitutes approximately 7.5% of all epithelial malignancies and 4% of all benign and malignant epithelial salivary gland tumors. The peak incidence for this tumor is reported to be in the fourth through sixth decades of life.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

17913</a>

1792]</p>

1793<p id="_230" tabindex="-1">

1794This neoplasm typically develops as a slow-growing swelling in the preauricular or submandibular region. Pain and facial paralysis develop frequently during the course of the disease and are likely related to the associated high incidence of nerve invasion.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

17953</a>

1796] For more information, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/pain/pain-hp-pdq">

1797Cancer Pain</a>

1798. Regardless of histological grade, adenoid cystic carcinomas, with their unusually slow biological growth, tend to have a protracted course and ultimately a poor outcome, with 10-year survival rates reported to be less than 50% for all grades.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

17991</a>

1800,<a href="#cit/section_2.27">

180127</a>

1802] These carcinomas typically show frequent recurrences and late distant metastases.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

18031</a>

1804,<a href="#cit/section_2.28">

180528</a>

1806] Clinical stage may be a better prognostic indicator than histological grade.[<a href="#cit/section_2.28">

180728</a>

1808,<a href="#cit/section_2.29">

180929</a>

1810] In a retrospective review of 92 cases, a tumor size larger than 4 cm was associated with an unfavorable clinical course in all cases.[<a href="#cit/section_2.30">

181130</a>

1812] </p>

1813</section>

1814<section id="_231">

1815<h5 id="_231_toc">

1816Adenocarcinomas</h5>

1817<section id="_291">

1818<h6 id="_291_toc">

1819Acinic cell carcinoma</h6>

1820<p id="_292" tabindex="-1">

1821Acinic cell carcinoma, also known as acinic cell adenocarcinoma, is a malignant epithelial neoplasm in which the neoplastic cells express acinar differentiation. By conventional use, the term acinic cell carcinoma is defined by cytologic differentiation toward serous acinar cells, as opposed to mucous acinar cells, whose characteristic feature is cytoplasmic PAS-positive zymogen-type secretory granules.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18223</a>

1823] In AFIP data of salivary gland neoplasms, acinic cell carcinoma is the third most common salivary gland epithelial neoplasm after mucoepidermoid carcinoma and adenocarcinoma, NOS.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18243</a>

1825] Acinic cell carcinoma accounted for 17% of primary malignant salivary gland tumors or about 6% of all salivary gland neoplasms. More than 80% of these tumors occur in the parotid gland, women were affected more than men, and the mean age was 44 years. Other studies have reported a relative frequency of acinic cell carcinoma from 0% to 19% of malignant salivary gland neoplasms.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18263</a>

1827]</p>

1828<p id="_293" tabindex="-1">

1829Clinically, patients typically present with a slowly enlarging mass in the parotid region. Pain is a symptom in more than 33% of patients. For acinic cell carcinoma, staging is likely a better predictor of outcome than histological grading.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18303</a>

1831] In a retrospective review of 90 cases, poor prognostic features included pain or fixation; gross

1832invasion; and microscopic features of desmoplasia, atypia, or increased mitotic activity. Neither morphological pattern nor cell composition was a predictive feature.[<a href="#cit/section_2.31">

183331</a>

1834] For more information, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/pain/pain-hp-pdq">

1835Cancer Pain</a>

1836. </p>

1837</section>

1838<section id="_294">

1839<h6 id="_294_toc">

1840PLGA</h6>

1841<p id="_295" tabindex="-1">

1842PLGA is a malignant epithelial tumor that is essentially limited to occurrence in minor salivary gland sites and is characterized by bland, uniform nuclear features; diverse but characteristic architecture; infiltrative growth; and perineural infiltration.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18433</a>

1844] In a series of 426 patients with minor salivary gland tumors, PLGA represented 11% of all tumors and 26% of those that were malignant.[<a href="#cit/section_2.32">

184532</a>

1846] In minor gland sites, PLGA is twice as frequent as adenoid cystic carcinoma, and among all benign and malignant salivary gland neoplasms, only pleomorphic adenoma and mucoepidermoid carcinoma are more common.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18473</a>

1848] In the AFIP case files, more than 60% of tumors occurred in the mucosa of either the soft or hard palates, approximately 16% occurred in the buccal mucosa, and 12% occurred in the upper lip. The average age of patients is reported to be 59 years, with 70% of patients between the ages of 50 and 79 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18493</a>

1850] The female-to-male ratio is about 2:1, a proportion greater than for malignant salivary gland tumors in general.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18513</a>

1852,<a href="#cit/section_2.33">

185333</a>

1854]</p>

1855<p id="_296" tabindex="-1">

1856PLGA typically presents as a firm, nontender swelling involving the mucosa of the hard and soft palates (i.e., it is often found at their junction), the cheek, or the upper lip. Discomfort, bleeding, telangiectasia, or ulceration of the overlying mucosa may occasionally occur.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18573</a>

1858] This salivary gland neoplasm typically runs a moderately indolent course. In a study of 40 cases with long-term follow-up, the overall survival rate was 80% at 25 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.34">

185934</a>

1860] Because of the unpredictable behavior of the tumor, some investigators consider the qualifying term, low grade, to be misleading and instead prefer the term polymorphous adenocarcinoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

18611</a>

1862]</p>

1863</section>

1864<section id="_297">

1865<h6 id="_297_toc">

1866Adenocarcinoma, NOS</h6>

1867<p id="_298" tabindex="-1">

1868Adenocarcinoma, NOS, is a salivary gland carcinoma that shows glandular or ductal differentiation but lacks the prominence of any of the morphological features that characterize the other, more specific carcinoma types. The diagnosis of adenocarcinoma, NOS, is essentially one of exclusion. In an AFIP review of cases, adenocarcinoma, NOS, was second only to mucoepidermoid carcinoma in frequency among malignant salivary gland neoplasms.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18693</a>

1870] Other series have reported an incidence of 4% to 10%.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

18711</a>

1872] In AFIP files, the mean patient age was 58 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18733</a>

1874] Approximately 40% and 60% of tumors occurred in the major and minor salivary glands, respectively. Among the major salivary gland tumors, 90% occurred in the parotid gland. Adenocarcinoma, NOS is graded in a similar way to extrasalivary lesions according to the degree of differentiation.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

18751</a>

1876] Tumor grades include low-grade, intermediate-grade, and high-grade categories.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18773</a>

1878]</p>

1879<p id="_299" tabindex="-1">

1880Patients with tumors in the major salivary glands typically present with solitary, painless masses.[<a href="#cit/section_2.35">

188135</a>

1882] Two retrospective studies indicate that survival is better for patients with tumors of the oral cavity than for those with tumors of the parotid and submandibular glands.[<a href="#cit/section_2.35">

188335</a>

1884,<a href="#cit/section_2.36">

188536</a>

1886] These studies differ regarding the prognostic significance of tumor grade.</p>

1887</section>

1888<section id="_300">

1889<h6 id="_300_toc">

1890Rare adenocarcinomas</h6>

1891<section id="_381">

1892<h6 id="_381_toc">

1893Basal cell adenocarcinoma</h6>

1894<p id="_242" tabindex="-1">

1895Basal cell adenocarcinoma, also known as basaloid salivary carcinoma, carcinoma ex monomorphic adenoma, malignant basal cell adenoma, malignant basal cell tumor, or basal cell carcinoma, is an epithelial neoplasm that is cytologically similar to basal cell adenoma but is infiltrative and has a small potential for metastasis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18963</a>

1897] In AFIP case files spanning almost 11 years, basal cell carcinoma made up 1.6% of all salivary gland neoplasms and 2.9% of salivary gland malignancies.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

18983</a>

1899] Nearly 90% of tumors occurred in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19003</a>

1901,<a href="#cit/section_2.37">

190237</a>

1903] The average age of patients was reported to be 60 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19043</a>

1905]</p>

1906<p id="_243" tabindex="-1">

1907Similar to most salivary gland neoplasms, swelling is typically the only sign or symptom.[<a href="#cit/section_2.37">

190837</a>

1909] A sudden increase in size may occur in a few patients.[<a href="#cit/section_2.38">

191038</a>

1911] Basal cell carcinomas are low-grade carcinomas that are infiltrative, locally destructive, and tend to recur. The carcinomas occasionally metastasize. In a retrospective series that included 29 patients, there were recurrences in 7 patients and metastases in 3 patients.[<a href="#cit/section_2.37">

191237</a>

1913] In another retrospective review that included 72 patients, 37% of the patients experienced local recurrences.[<a href="#cit/section_2.38">

191438</a>

1915] The overall prognosis for patients with this tumor is good.[<a href="#cit/section_2.37">

191637</a>

1917,<a href="#cit/section_2.38">

191838</a>

1919]</p>

1920</section>

1921<section id="_382">

1922<h6 id="_382_toc">

1923Clear cell carcinoma</h6>

1924<p id="_244" tabindex="-1">

1925Clear cell carcinoma, also known as clear cell adenocarcinoma, is a very rare malignant epithelial neoplasm composed of a monomorphous population of cells that have optically clear cytoplasm with standard hematoxylin and eosin stains and lack features of other specific neoplasms. Because of inconsistencies in the methods of reporting salivary gland neoplasms, meaningful incidence rates for this tumor are difficult to derive from the literature.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19263</a>

1927] Most cases involve the minor salivary glands.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

19281</a>

1929,<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19303</a>

1931,<a href="#cit/section_2.39">

193239</a>

1933-<a href="#cit/section_2.41">

193441</a>

1935] In the AFIP case files, the mean age of patients was approximately 58 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19363</a>

1937]</p>

1938<p id="_245" tabindex="-1">

1939In most patients, swelling is the only symptom. Clear cell adenocarcinoma is a low-grade neoplasm. As of 1996, the AFIP reported that no patient had died of this tumor.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19403</a>

1941]</p>

1942</section>

1943<section id="_383">

1944<h6 id="_383_toc">

1945Cystadenocarcinoma</h6>

1946<p id="_246" tabindex="-1">

1947Cystadenocarcinoma is a rare malignant epithelial tumor characterized histologically by prominent cystic and, frequently, papillary growth but lacking features that characterize cystic variants of several more common salivary gland neoplasms. It is also known as malignant papillary cystadenoma, mucus-producing adenopapillary, or nonepidermoid, carcinoma; low-grade papillary adenocarcinoma of the palate; or papillary adenocarcinoma. Cystadenocarcinoma is the malignant counterpart of cystadenoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19483</a>

1949] </p>

1950<p id="_247" tabindex="-1">

1951In a review that included 57 patients, the AFIP found that men and women are affected equally. The

1952average patient age was approximately 59 years. Approximately 65% of the tumors occurred in the major salivary glands, primarily in the parotid.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19533</a>

1954] Most patients present with a slow-growing asymptomatic mass. Clinically, this neoplasm is rarely associated with pain or facial paralysis. Cystadenocarcinoma is considered to be a low-grade neoplasm.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19553</a>

1956]</p>

1957</section>

1958<section id="_384">

1959<h6 id="_384_toc">

1960Sebaceous adenocarcinoma</h6>

1961<p id="_248" tabindex="-1">

1962 Sebaceous adenocarcinoma is a rare malignant epithelial tumor composed of islands and sheets of cells that have morphologically atypical nuclei, an infiltrative growth pattern, and focal sebaceous differentiation. This is a very rare tumor, as few cases have been reported in the literature.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19633</a>

1964] Almost all cases occur in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19653</a>

1966] The average age of patients is reported to be 69 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.42">

196742</a>

1968]</p>

1969<p id="_249" tabindex="-1">

1970An equal number of patients present with a painless, slow-growing, asymptomatic swelling or pain. A few experience facial paralysis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19713</a>

1972] Most sebaceous adenocarcinomas are probably intermediate-grade malignancies. The tumor recurs in about 33% of cases.[<a href="#cit/section_2.43">

197343</a>

1974,<a href="#cit/section_2.44">

197544</a>

1976]</p>

1977</section>

1978<section id="_385">

1979<h6 id="_385_toc">

1980Sebaceous lymphadenocarcinoma</h6>

1981<p id="_250" tabindex="-1">

1982Sebaceous lymphadenocarcinoma is an extremely rare malignant tumor that represents carcinomatous transformation of sebaceous lymphadenoma. The carcinoma element may be sebaceous adenocarcinoma or some other specific or nonspecific form of salivary gland cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19833</a>

1984] Only three cases have been reported in the literature.[<a href="#cit/section_2.43">

198543</a>

1986,<a href="#cit/section_2.45">

198745</a>

1988] The three cases occurred in or around the parotid gland. All patients were in their seventh decade of life. Two of the three patients were asymptomatic. One had tenderness on palpation. Case reports suggest that this is a low-grade malignancy with a good prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.44">

198944</a>

1990,<a href="#cit/section_2.45">

199145</a>

1992]</p>

1993</section>

1994<section id="_386">

1995<h6 id="_386_toc">

1996Oncocytic carcinoma</h6>

1997<p id="_251" tabindex="-1">

1998Oncocytic carcinoma, also known as oncocytic adenocarcinoma, is a rare, predominantly oncocytic neoplasm whose malignant nature is reflected both by its abnormal morphological features and infiltrative growth. Oncocytic carcinoma represents less than 1% of almost 3,100 salivary gland tumors accessioned to the AFIP files during a 10-year period.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

19993</a>

2000] Most cases occur in the parotid gland. The average age of patients in the AFIP series was 63 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20013</a>

2002]</p>

2003<p id="_252" tabindex="-1">

2004Approximately 33% of the patients usually develop parotid masses that cause pain or paralysis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.46">

200546</a>

2006] Oncocytic carcinoma is a high-grade carcinoma. Patients with tumors smaller than 2 cm have a better prognosis than patients with larger tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_2.6">

20076</a>

2008]</p>

2009</section>

2010<section id="_387">

2011<h6 id="_387_toc">

2012Salivary duct carcinoma</h6>

2013<p id="_253" tabindex="-1">

2014Salivary duct carcinoma, also known as salivary duct adenocarcinoma, is a rare, typically high-grade malignant epithelial neoplasm composed of structures that resemble expanded salivary gland ducts. A low-grade variant exists.[<a href="#cit/section_2.47">

201547</a>

2016] Incidence rates vary depending on the study cited.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20173</a>

2018] In the AFIP files, salivary duct carcinomas represent only 0.2% of all epithelial salivary gland neoplasms. More than 85% of cases involve the parotid gland, and approximately 75% of patients are men. The peak incidence is reported to be in the seventh and eighth decades of life.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20193</a>

2020]</p>

2021<p id="_254" tabindex="-1">

2022Clinically, parotid swelling is the most common sign. Facial nerve dysfunction or paralysis occur in more than 25% of patients and may be the initial manifestation.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20233</a>

2024] The high-grade variant of this neoplasm is one of the most aggressive types of salivary gland carcinoma and is typified by local invasion, lymphatic and hematogenous spread, and poor prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20253</a>

2026,<a href="#cit/section_2.7">

20277</a>

2028] In a retrospective review of 104 cases, 33% of patients developed local recurrence, and 46% of patients developed distant metastasis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.48">

202948</a>

2030]</p>

2031</section>

2032<section id="_388">

2033<h6 id="_388_toc">

2034Mucinous adenocarcinoma</h6>

2035<p id="_255" tabindex="-1">

2036Mucinous adenocarcinoma is a rare malignant neoplasm characterized by large amounts of extracellular epithelial mucin that contains cords, nests, and solitary epithelial cells. The incidence is unknown. Limited data indicate that most, if not all, occur in the major salivary glands, with the submandibular gland as the predominant site.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20373</a>

2038,<a href="#cit/section_2.49">

203949</a>

2040] These tumors may be associated with dull pain and tenderness.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20413</a>

2042,<a href="#cit/section_2.49">

204349</a>

2044] This neoplasm may be considered low grade.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20453</a>

2046]</p>

2047</section>

2048</section>

2049</section>

2050<section id="_256">

2051<h5 id="_256_toc">

2052Malignant mixed tumors</h5>

2053<p id="_257" tabindex="-1">

2054The classification of malignant mixed tumors includes three distinct clinicopathological entities: carcinoma ex pleomorphic adenoma, carcinosarcoma, and metastasizing mixed tumor. Carcinoma ex pleomorphic adenoma accounts for most cases, whereas carcinosarcoma, a true malignant mixed tumor, and metastasizing mixed tumor are extremely rare.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20553</a>

2056]</p>

2057<section id="_301">

2058<h6 id="_301_toc">

2059Carcinoma ex pleomorphic adenoma</h6>

2060<p id="_258" tabindex="-1">

2061Carcinoma ex pleomorphic adenoma, also known as carcinoma ex mixed tumor, shows histological evidence of arising from or in a benign pleomorphic adenoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.50">

206250</a>

2063] Diagnosis requires the identification of benign tumor in the tissue sample.[<a href="#cit/section_2.51">

206451</a>

2065] The incidence or relative frequency of this tumor varies considerably depending on the study cited.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

20661</a>

2067] A review of material at the AFIP showed that carcinoma ex pleomorphic adenoma makes up 8.8% of all mixed tumors and 4.6% of all malignant salivary gland tumors. It is ranked as the sixth most common malignant salivary gland tumor after mucoepidermoid carcinoma; adenocarcinoma, NOS; acinic cell carcinoma; polymorphous low-grade adenocarcinoma; and adenoid cystic carcinoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20683</a>

2069] The neoplasm occurs primarily in the major salivary glands.[<a href="#cit/section_2.52">

207052</a>

2071]</p>

2072<p id="_259" tabindex="-1">

2073The most common clinical presentation is a painless mass.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20743</a>

2075] Approximately 33% of patients may experience facial paralysis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.53">

207653</a>

2077] Depending on the series cited, survival rates vary significantly: 25% to 65% at 5 years, 24% to 50% at 10 years, 10% to 35% at 15 years, and 0% to 38% at 20 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20783</a>

2079] In addition to tumor stage, histological grade and degree of invasion help to determine prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.54">

208054</a>

2081]</p>

2082</section>

2083<section id="_302">

2084<h6 id="_302_toc">

2085Carcinosarcoma</h6>

2086<p id="_260" tabindex="-1">

2087Carcinosarcoma, also known as true malignant mixed tumor, is a rare malignant salivary gland neoplasm that contains both carcinoma and sarcoma components. Either or both components are expressed in metastatic foci. Some carcinosarcomas develop de novo, while others develop in association with benign mixed tumor. This neoplasm is rare; only eight cases exist in the AFIP case files.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

20883</a>

2089] At one facility, only 11 cases were recorded over a 32-year period.[<a href="#cit/section_2.8">

20908</a>

2091] Most of these tumors occur in the major salivary glands.</p>

2092<p id="_261" tabindex="-1">

2093Swelling, pain, nerve palsy, and ulceration have been frequent clinical findings. Carcinosarcoma is an aggressive, high-grade malignancy. In the largest series reported, which consisted of 12 cases, the average survival period was 3.6 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.8">

20948</a>

2095]</p>

2096</section>

2097<section id="_303">

2098<h6 id="_303_toc">

2099Metastasizing mixed tumor</h6>

2100<p id="_262" tabindex="-1">

2101Metastasizing mixed tumor is a very rare, histologically benign salivary gland neoplasm that inexplicably metastasizes. Often a long interval occurs between the diagnosis of the primary tumor and the metastases. The histological features are within the spectrum of features that typify pleomorphic adenoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21023</a>

2103] The majority occur in the major salivary glands. The primary neoplasm is typically a single, well-defined mass. Recurrences, which may be multiple, have been reported to occur for as many as 26 years after excision of the primary neoplasm.[<a href="#cit/section_2.55">

210455</a>

2105]</p>

2106</section>

2107</section>

2108<section id="_306">

2109<h5 id="_306_toc">

2110Rare carcinomas</h5>

2111<section id="_307">

2112<h6 id="_307_toc">

2113Primary squamous cell carcinoma</h6>

2114<p id="_265" tabindex="-1">

2115Primary squamous cell carcinoma, also known as primary epidermoid carcinoma, is a malignant epithelial neoplasm of the major salivary glands that is composed of squamous (i.e., epidermoid) cells. Diagnosis requires the exclusion of primary disease located in some other head and neck site; indeed, most squamous cell carcinomas of the major salivary glands represent metastatic disease.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21163</a>

2117] This diagnosis is not made in minor salivary glands because distinction from the more common mucosal squamous cell carcinoma is not possible.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21183</a>

2119] Previous exposure to ionizing radiation appears to increase the risk of developing this neoplasm.[<a href="#cit/section_2.11">

212011</a>

2121,<a href="#cit/section_2.56">

212256</a>

2123,<a href="#cit/section_2.57">

212457</a>

2125] The median time between radiation therapy and diagnosis of the neoplasm is approximately 15.5 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.11">

212611</a>

2127] The reported frequency of this tumor among all major salivary gland tumors has varied from 0.9% to 4.7%.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21283</a>

2129,<a href="#cit/section_2.10">

213010</a>

2131] In AFIP major salivary gland accessions from 1985 to 1996, primary squamous cell carcinoma accounted for 2.7% of all tumors; 5.4% of malignant tumors; and 2.5% and 2.8%, respectively, of all parotid and submandibular tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21323</a>

2133] The average age in the AFIP registry was 64 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21343</a>

2135] This neoplasm occurs in the parotid gland almost nine times more often than in the submandibular gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21363</a>

2137,<a href="#cit/section_2.57">

213857</a>

2139] There is a strong male predilection.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21403</a>

2141,<a href="#cit/section_2.11">

214211</a>

2143,<a href="#cit/section_2.57">

214457</a>

2145-<a href="#cit/section_2.59">

214659</a>

2147] This tumor is graded in a similar way to extrasalivary lesions according to the degree of differentiation, namely, low grade, intermediate grade, and high grade.[<a href="#cit/section_2.1">

21481</a>

2149]</p>

2150<p id="_266" tabindex="-1">

2151Most patients present with an asymptomatic mass in the parotid region. Other symptoms may include a painful mass and facial nerve palsy.[<a href="#cit/section_2.57">

215257</a>

2153] The prognosis for this neoplasm is poor. In a 30-year retrospective analysis of 50 cases of squamous cell carcinoma of the salivary glands, survival rates at 5 years and 10 years were 24% and 18%, respectively.[<a href="#cit/section_2.57">

215457</a>

2155]</p>

2156</section>

2157<section id="_308">

2158<h6 id="_308_toc">

2159Epithelial-myoepithelial carcinoma</h6>

2160<p id="_268" tabindex="-1">

2161Epithelial-myoepithelial carcinoma is an uncommon, low-grade epithelial neoplasm composed of variable proportions of ductal and large, clear-staining, differentiated myoepithelial cells. It is also known as adenomyoepithelioma, clear cell adenoma, tubular solid adenoma, monomorphic clear cell tumor, glycogen-rich adenoma, glycogen-rich adenocarcinoma, clear cell carcinoma, or salivary duct carcinoma. The tumor represents approximately 1% of all epithelial salivary gland neoplasms.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21623</a>

2163,<a href="#cit/section_2.60">

216460</a>

2165] It is predominantly a tumor of the parotid gland. In the AFIP case files, the mean age of patients was about 60 years, and about 60% of the patients were female.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

21663</a>

2167]</p>

2168<p id="_269" tabindex="-1">

2169Localized swelling is commonly the only symptom, but occasionally patients experience facial weakness or pain.[<a href="#cit/section_2.61">

217061</a>

2171,<a href="#cit/section_2.62">

217262</a>

2173] Overall, epithelial-myoepithelial carcinoma is a low-grade carcinoma that recurs frequently, has a tendency to metastasize to periparotid and cervical lymph nodes, and occasionally results in distant metastasis and death.[<a href="#cit/section_2.60">

217460</a>

2175,<a href="#cit/section_2.62">

217662</a>

2177-<a href="#cit/section_2.64">

217864</a>

2179]</p>

2180</section>

2181<section id="_309">

2182<h6 id="_309_toc">

2183Anaplastic small cell carcinoma</h6>

2184<p id="_271" tabindex="-1">

2185Anaplastic small cell carcinoma of the salivary glands was first described in 1972.[<a href="#cit/section_2.65">

218665</a>

2187] Subsequent histochemical and electron microscopic studies have supported the neuroendocrine nature of this tumor.[<a href="#cit/section_2.66">

218866</a>

2189,<a href="#cit/section_2.67">

219067</a>

2191] Microscopically, the tumor cells have oval, hyperchromatic nuclei and a scant amount of cytoplasm and are organized in sheets, strands, and nests. The mitotic rate is high. Neuroendocrine carcinomas are more frequently found in the minor salivary glands. These patients have a better survival rate than patients with small cell carcinomas of the lung.[<a href="#cit/section_2.68">

219268</a>

2193] The undifferentiated counterpart of this neoplasm is the small cell undifferentiated carcinoma. </p>

2194</section>

2195<section id="_310">

2196<h6 id="_310_toc">

2197Undifferentiated carcinomas</h6>

2198<p id="_273" tabindex="-1">

2199Undifferentiated carcinomas of salivary glands are a group of uncommon malignant epithelial neoplasms that lack the specific light-microscopic morphological features of other types of salivary gland carcinomas. These carcinomas are histologically similar to undifferentiated carcinomas that arise in other organs and tissues. Accordingly, metastatic carcinoma is a primary concern in the differential diagnosis of these neoplasms.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22003</a>

2201]</p>

2202<section id="_389">

2203<h6 id="_389_toc">

2204Small cell undifferentiated carcinoma</h6>

2205<p id="_274" tabindex="-1">

2206Small cell undifferentiated carcinoma, also known as extrapulmonary oat cell carcinoma, is a rare, primary malignant tumor. With conventional light microscopy, it is composed of undifferentiated cells and, with ultrastructural or immunohistochemical studies, does not demonstrate neuroendocrine

2207differentiation. This is the undifferentiated counterpart of anaplastic small cell carcinoma. For more information, see the <a href="/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq#_309">

2208Anaplastic small cell carcinoma </a>

2209 section. </p>

2210<p id="_275" tabindex="-1">

2211In an AFIP review of case files, small cell carcinoma represented 1.8% of all major salivary gland malignancies; the mean age of patients was 56 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22123</a>

2213] In 50% of the cases, patients present with an asymptomatic parotid mass of 3 months' or less duration.[<a href="#cit/section_2.68">

221468</a>

2215-<a href="#cit/section_2.70">

221670</a>

2217] This is a high-grade neoplasm. In a retrospective review of 12 cases, a tumor size of more than 4 cm was found to be the most important predictor of behavior. In another small retrospective series, estimated survival rates at 2 and 5 years were 70% and 46%, respectively.[<a href="#cit/section_2.68">

221868</a>

2219]</p>

2220</section>

2221<section id="_390">

2222<h6 id="_390_toc">

2223Large cell undifferentiated carcinoma</h6>

2224<p id="_276" tabindex="-1">

2225Large cell undifferentiated carcinoma is a tumor in which features of acinar, ductal, epidermoid, or myoepithelial differentiation are absent under light microscopy, though occasionally, poorly formed duct-like structures are found. This neoplasm accounts for approximately 1% of all epithelial salivary gland neoplasms.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22263</a>

2227,<a href="#cit/section_2.53">

222853</a>

2229,<a href="#cit/section_2.71">

223071</a>

2231,<a href="#cit/section_2.72">

223272</a>

2233] Most of these tumors occur in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.70">

223470</a>

2235,<a href="#cit/section_2.72">

223672</a>

2237] In AFIP data, the peak incidence is in the seventh to eighth decades of life.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22383</a>

2239]</p>

2240<p id="_277" tabindex="-1">

2241Rapid growth of a parotid swelling is a common clinical presentation.[<a href="#cit/section_2.59">

224259</a>

2243] This is a high-grade neoplasm that frequently metastasizes and has a poor prognosis. Patients with neoplasms of 4 cm or larger may have a particularly poor outcome.[<a href="#cit/section_2.70">

224470</a>

2245,<a href="#cit/section_2.72">

224672</a>

2247]</p>

2248</section>

2249<section id="_391">

2250<h6 id="_391_toc">

2251Lymphoepithelial carcinoma</h6>

2252<p id="_278" tabindex="-1">

2253Lymphoepithelial carcinoma, also known as undifferentiated carcinoma with lymphoid stroma and carcinoma ex lymphoepithelial lesion, is an undifferentiated tumor that is associated with a dense lymphoid stroma. An exceptionally high incidence of this tumor is found in the Inuit population.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22543</a>

2255,<a href="#cit/section_2.73">

225673</a>

2257] This neoplasm has been associated with Epstein-Barr virus infection.[<a href="#cit/section_2.74">

225874</a>

2259,<a href="#cit/section_2.75">

226075</a>

2261] Of the occurrences, 80% are in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22623</a>

2263]</p>

2264<p id="_279" tabindex="-1">

2265In addition to the presence of a parotid or submandibular mass, pain is a frequent symptom, and facial nerve palsy occurs in as many as 20% of patients.[<a href="#cit/section_2.76">

226676</a>

2267] Of the patients, more than 40% have metastases to cervical lymph nodes at initial presentation, 20% develop local recurrences or lymph node metastases, and 20% develop distant metastases within 3 years following therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_2.73">

226873</a>

2269,<a href="#cit/section_2.76">

227076</a>

2271-<a href="#cit/section_2.78">

227278</a>

2273] For more information, see <a href="/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects/pain/pain-hp-pdq">

2274Cancer Pain</a>

2275. </p>

2276</section>

2277</section>

2278<section id="_311">

2279<h6 id="_311_toc">

2280Myoepithelial carcinoma</h6>

2281<p id="_281" tabindex="-1">

2282Myoepithelioma carcinoma is a rare, malignant salivary gland neoplasm in which the tumor cells almost exclusively manifest myoepithelial differentiation. This neoplasm represents the malignant counterpart of benign myoepithelioma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22833</a>

2284] To date, the largest series reported involves 25 cases.[<a href="#cit/section_2.79">

228579</a>

2286] Approximately 66% of the tumors occur in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22873</a>

2288,<a href="#cit/section_2.74">

228974</a>

2290] The mean age of patients is reported to be 55 years.[<a href="#cit/section_2.79">

229179</a>

2292]</p>

2293<p id="_282" tabindex="-1">

2294Most patients present with the primary complaint of a painless mass.[<a href="#cit/section_2.79">

229579</a>

2296] This is an intermediate grade to high-grade carcinoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

22973</a>

2298,<a href="#cit/section_2.79">

229979</a>

2300] Histological grade does not appear to correlate well with clinical behavior; tumors with a low-grade histological appearance may behave aggressively.[<a href="#cit/section_2.79">

230179</a>

2302]</p>

2303</section>

2304<section id="_312">

2305<h6 id="_312_toc">

2306Adenosquamous carcinoma</h6>

2307<p id="_284" tabindex="-1">

2308Adenosquamous carcinoma is an extremely rare malignant neoplasm that simultaneously arises from surface mucosal epithelium and salivary gland ductal epithelium. The carcinoma shows histopathological features of both squamous cell carcinoma and adenocarcinoma. Only a handful of reports describe this tumor.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

23093</a>

2310]</p>

2311<p id="_285" tabindex="-1">

2312In addition to swelling, adenosquamous carcinoma produces visible changes in the mucosa, including erythema, ulceration, and induration. Pain frequently accompanies ulceration. Limited data indicate that this is a highly aggressive neoplasm with a poor prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

23133</a>

2314]</p>

2315</section>

2316</section>

2317</section>

2318</section>

2319<section id="_192">

2320<h3 id="_192_toc">

2321Nonepithelial Neoplasms</h3>

2322<p id="_193" tabindex="-1">

2323<strong>

2324Lymphomas and benign lymphoepithelial lesion</strong>

2325</p>

2326<p id="_194" tabindex="-1">

2327Lymphomas of the major salivary glands are characteristically of the non-Hodgkin type. In an AFIP review of case files, non-Hodgkin lymphoma accounted for 16.3% of all malignant tumors that occurred in the major salivary glands; disease in the parotid gland accounted for about 80% of all cases.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

23283</a>

2329]</p>

2330<p id="_195" tabindex="-1">

2331Patients with benign lymphoepithelial lesion (e.g., Mikulicz disease), which is a manifestation of the autoimmune disease Sj&#246;gren syndrome, are at an increased risk for development of non-Hodgkin lymphoma.[<a href="#cit/section_2.80">

233280</a>

2333-<a href="#cit/section_2.84">

233484</a>

2335] Benign lymphoepithelial lesion is clinically characterized by diffuse and bilateral enlargement of the salivary and lacrimal glands.[<a href="#cit/section_2.23">

233623</a>

2337] Morphologically, a salivary gland lesion is composed of prominent myoepithelial islands surrounded by a lymphocytic infiltrate. Germinal centers are often present in the lymphocytic infiltrate.[<a href="#cit/section_2.23">

233823</a>

2339] Immunophenotypically and genotypically, the lymphocytic infiltrate is composed of B-lymphocytes and T-lymphocytes, which are polyclonal. In

2340some instances, the B-cell lymphocytic infiltrate can undergo clonal expansion and evolve into frank non-Hodgkin lymphoma. The vast majority of the non-Hodgkin lymphomas arising in a background of benign lymphoepithelial lesions are marginal zone lymphomas of mucosa-associated lymphoid tissue (MALT).[<a href="#cit/section_2.81">

234181</a>

2342-<a href="#cit/section_2.84">

234384</a>

2344] MALT lymphomas of the salivary glands, like their counterparts in other anatomical sites, typically display relatively indolent clinical behavior.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

23453</a>

2346,<a href="#cit/section_2.85">

234785</a>

2348] </p>

2349<p id="_196" tabindex="-1">

2350Primary non-MALT lymphomas of the salivary glands may also occur and appear to have a prognosis similar to those in patients who have histologically identical nodal lymphomas.[<a href="#cit/section_2.86">

235186</a>

2352,<a href="#cit/section_2.87">

235387</a>

2354] Unlike non-Hodgkin lymphoma, involvement of the major salivary glands by Hodgkin lymphoma is rare. Most tumors occur in the parotid gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

23553</a>

2356] The most common histological types encountered are the nodular sclerosing and lymphocyte-predominant variants.[<a href="#cit/section_2.88">

235788</a>

2358,<a href="#cit/section_2.89">

235989</a>

2360]</p>

2361<p id="_197" tabindex="-1">

2362<strong>

2363Mesenchymal neoplasms</strong>

2364</p>

2365<p id="_198" tabindex="-1">

2366Mesenchymal neoplasms account for 1.9% to 5% of all neoplasms that occur within the major salivary glands.[<a href="#cit/section_2.90">

236790</a>

2368,<a href="#cit/section_2.91">

236991</a>

2370] These cellular classifications pertain to major salivary gland tumors. Because the minor salivary glands are small and embedded within fibrous connective tissue, fat, and skeletal muscle, the origin of a mesenchymal neoplasm from stroma cannot be determined.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

23713</a>

2372] The types of benign mesenchymal salivary gland neoplasms include hemangiomas, lipomas, and lymphangiomas. </p>

2373<p id="_199" tabindex="-1">

2374Malignant mesenchymal salivary gland neoplasms include malignant schwannomas, hemangiopericytomas, malignant fibrous histiocytomas, rhabdomyosarcomas, and fibrosarcomas, among others. In the major salivary glands, these neoplasms represent approximately 0.5% of all benign and malignant salivary gland tumors and approximately 1.5% of all malignant tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_2.90">

237590</a>

2376,<a href="#cit/section_2.92">

237792</a>

2378,<a href="#cit/section_2.93">

237993</a>

2380] It is important to establish a primary salivary gland origin for these tumors by excluding the possibilities of metastasis and direct extension from other sites. In addition, the diagnosis of salivary gland carcinosarcoma should be excluded.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

23813</a>

2382] Primary salivary gland sarcomas behave like their soft tissue counterparts, in which prognosis is related to sarcoma type, histological grade, tumor size, and stage.[<a href="#cit/section_2.93">

238393</a>

2384,<a href="#cit/section_2.94">

238594</a>

2386] For more information, see <a href="/types/soft-tissue-sarcoma/hp/adult-soft-tissue-treatment-pdq">

2387Soft Tissue Sarcoma Treatment</a>

2388. A comprehensive review of salivary gland mesenchymal neoplasms can be found elsewhere.[<a href="#cit/section_2.95">

238995</a>

2390]</p>

2391</section>

2392<section id="_200">

2393<h3 id="_200_toc">

2394Malignant Secondary Neoplasms</h3>

2395<p id="_201" tabindex="-1">

2396Malignant neoplasms whose origins lie outside the salivary glands may involve the major salivary glands by:[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

23973</a>

2398] </p>

2399<div class="pdq-content-list">

2400<ol id="_209">

2401<li>

2402Direct invasion from cancers that lie adjacent to the salivary glands.</li>

2403<li>

2404Hematogenous metastases from distant primary tumors. </li>

2405<li>

2406Lymphatic metastases to lymph nodes within the salivary gland.</li>

2407</ol>

2408</div>

2409<p id="_210" tabindex="-1">

2410 Direct invasion of nonsalivary gland tumors into the major salivary glands is principally from squamous cell and basal cell carcinomas of the overlying skin.</p>

2411<p id="_202" tabindex="-1">

2412Approximately 80% of metastases to the major salivary glands may be from primary tumors elsewhere in the head and neck; the remaining 20% may be from infraclavicular sites.[<a href="#cit/section_2.96">

241396</a>

2414,<a href="#cit/section_2.97">

241597</a>

2416] The parotid gland is the site of 80% to 90% of the metastases, and the remainder involve the submandibular gland.[<a href="#cit/section_2.97">

241797</a>

2418,<a href="#cit/section_2.98">

241998</a>

2420] In a decade-long AFIP experience, metastatic tumors constituted approximately 10% of malignant neoplasms in the major salivary glands, exclusive of malignant lymphomas.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

24213</a>

2422] Most metastatic primary tumors to the major salivary glands are squamous cell carcinomas and melanomas from the head and neck that presumably reach the parotid gland via the lymphatic system; infraclavicular primary tumors, such as the lung, kidney, and breast, reach the salivary glands by a hematogenous route.[<a href="#cit/section_2.97">

242397</a>

2424-<a href="#cit/section_2.99">

242599</a>

2426] The peak incidence for metastatic tumors in the salivary glands is reported to be in the seventh decade of life.[<a href="#cit/section_2.3">

24273</a>

2428]</p>

2429</section>

2809

2810 <section id="_13">

2811

2812 <h2>

2813Stage Information for Salivary Gland Cancer</h2>

2814

2815 <div id="_section_13" class="pdq-sections">

2816<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

2817<h6>

2818In This Section</h6>

2819<ul>

2820<li>

2821<a href="#_375_toc">

2822American Joint Committee on Cancer (AJCC) Stage Groupings and TNM Definitions</a>

2823</li>

2824</ul>

2825</nav>

2826<p id="_14" tabindex="-1">

2827In general, tumors of the major salivary glands are staged according to size, extraparenchymal extension, lymph node involvement (in parotid tumors, whether or not the facial nerve is involved), and presence of metastases.[<a href="#cit/section_3.1">

28281</a>

2829-<a href="#cit/section_3.4">

28304</a>

2831]

2832Tumors arising in the minor salivary glands are staged according to the anatomical site of origin (e.g., oral cavity and sinuses).

2833</p>

2834<p id="_340" tabindex="-1">

2835Clinical stage, particularly tumor size, may be the critical factor in determining the outcome of salivary gland cancer and may be more important than histological grade.[<a href="#cit/section_3.5">

28365</a>

2837,<a href="#cit/section_3.6">

28386</a>

2839] Diagnostic imaging studies may be used in staging. With excellent spatial resolution and superior soft tissue contrast, magnetic resonance imaging

2840(MRI) offers advantages over computed tomographic scanning in the

2841detection and localization of head and neck tumors. Overall, MRI is the preferred modality for evaluation of suspected neoplasms of the salivary glands.[<a href="#cit/section_3.7">

28427</a>

2843]</p>

2844<section id="_375">

2845<h3 id="_375_toc">

2846American Joint Committee on Cancer (AJCC) Stage Groupings and TNM Definitions</h3>

2847<p id="_374" tabindex="-1">

2848The AJCC has designated staging by TNM

2849(tumor, node, metastasis) classification to define salivary gland cancer.[<a href="#cit/section_3.5">

28505</a>

2851]</p>

3456 <section id="_42">

3457

3458 <h2>

3459Treatment Option Overview</h2>

3460

3461 <div id="_section_42" class="pdq-sections">

3462<p id="_43" tabindex="-1">

3463The minimum therapy for patients with low-grade malignancies of the superficial portion of

3464the parotid gland is a superficial parotidectomy. For all other lesions, a

3465total parotidectomy is often indicated. The facial nerve or its branches

3466should be resected if involved by tumor; repair can be done simultaneously.

3467Growing evidence suggests that postoperative radiation therapy augments

3468surgical resection, particularly for the high-grade neoplasms, when margins

3469are close or involved, when tumors are large, or when histological evidence of lymph node metastases is present.[<a href="#cit/section_4.1">

34701</a>

3471-<a href="#cit/section_4.8">

34728</a>

3473] Clinical trials in the United

3474States and England indicated that fast neutron-beam radiation therapy improves

3475disease-free survival and overall survival in patients with unresectable tumors or for patients with recurrent neoplasms.[<a href="#cit/section_4.9">

34769</a>

3477-<a href="#cit/section_4.12">

347812</a>

3479] Facilities with fast neutron-beam

3480radiation therapy are of limited availability in the United States. Accelerated hyperfractionated

3481photon-beam radiation therapy has also resulted in high rates of long-term

3482local regional controls.[<a href="#cit/section_4.13">

348313</a>

3484,<a href="#cit/section_4.14">

348514</a>

3486] The use of chemotherapy for malignant salivary

3487gland tumors remains under evaluation.[<a href="#cit/section_4.15">

348815</a>

3489-<a href="#cit/section_4.19">

349019</a>

3491]

3492</p>

3591<section id="_49">

3592<h3 id="_49_toc">

3593Treatment Options for Low-Grade Stage I Major Salivary Gland Tumors</h3>

3594<p id="_440" tabindex="-1">

3595Treatment options for low-grade stage I major salivary gland tumors include the following:</p>

3596<div class="pdq-content-list">

3597<ol id="_315">

3598<li>

3599Surgery alone.

3600</li>

3601<li>

3602Postoperative radiation therapy should be considered when the resection margins are positive.</li>

3603</ol>

3604</div>

3605<p id="_441" tabindex="-1">

3606Low-grade stage I tumors of the salivary gland are curable with surgery

3607alone.[<a href="#cit/section_5.1">

36081</a>

3609-<a href="#cit/section_5.3">

36103</a>

3611] Radiation therapy may be used for tumors for which resection

3612involves a significant cosmetic or functional deficit or as an adjuvant to

3613surgery when positive margins are present.[<a href="#cit/section_5.4">

36144</a>

3615] Neutron-beam therapy is

3616effective in the treatment of patients with malignant salivary gland

3617tumors with a poor prognosis.[<a href="#cit/section_5.5">

36185</a>

3619-<a href="#cit/section_5.7">

36207</a>

3621]</p>

3622</section>

3623<section id="_52">

3624<h3 id="_52_toc">

3625Treatment Options for High-Grade Stage I Major Salivary Gland Tumors</h3>

3626<p id="_442" tabindex="-1">

3627Treatment options for high-grade stage I major salivary gland tumors include the following:</p>

3628<div class="pdq-content-list">

3629<ol id="_100">

3630<li>

3631Localized high-grade salivary gland tumors that are confined to the gland in

3632which they arise may be cured by radical surgery alone.

3633</li>

3634<li>

3635Postoperative radiation therapy may improve local control and increase

3636survival rates for patients with high-grade tumors, positive surgical

3637margins, or perineural invasion.[<a href="#cit/section_5.8">

36388</a>

3639][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3640Level of evidence C2</a>

3641]; [<a href="#cit/section_5.9">

36429</a>

3643-<a href="#cit/section_5.11">

364411</a>

3645]

3646</li>

3647<li>

3648Chemotherapy (under clinical evaluation).[<a href="#cit/section_5.12">

364912</a>

3650,<a href="#cit/section_5.13">

365113</a>

3652]</li>

3653</ol>

3654</div>

3655<p id="_436" tabindex="-1">

3656Clinical trials exploring newer methods of local control are appropriate. </p>

3657<p id="_443" tabindex="-1">

3658High-grade stage I salivary gland tumors that are confined to the gland in

3659which they arise may be cured by surgery alone, although adjuvant radiation

3660therapy may be used, especially with the presence of positive margins.</p>

3661</section>

3756<section id="_62">

3757<h3 id="_62_toc">

3758Treatment Options for Low-Grade Stage II Major Salivary Gland Tumors</h3>

3759<p id="_444" tabindex="-1">

3760Treatment options for low-grade stage II major salivary gland tumors include the following:</p>

3761<div class="pdq-content-list">

3762<ol id="_102">

3763<li>

3764Surgery alone or with postoperative radiation therapy, if indicated, is appropriate.[<a href="#cit/section_6.1">

37651</a>

3766,<a href="#cit/section_6.2">

37672</a>

3768]</li>

3769<li>

3770Chemotherapy should be considered in special circumstances, such as when radiation

3771therapy or surgery is refused.</li>

3772</ol>

3773</div>

3774<p id="_445" tabindex="-1">

3775Low-grade stage II tumors of the salivary gland may be cured with surgery

3776alone.[<a href="#cit/section_6.3">

37773</a>

3778-<a href="#cit/section_6.5">

37795</a>

3780] Radiation therapy may be used as primary

3781treatment for tumors for in which resection involves a significant

3782cosmetic or functional deficit or as an adjuvant to surgery when positive

3783margins are present.[<a href="#cit/section_6.6">

37846</a>

3785]</p>

3786</section>

3787<section id="_66">

3788<h3 id="_66_toc">

3789Treatment Options for High-Grade Stage II Major Salivary Gland Tumors</h3>

3790<p id="_446" tabindex="-1">

3791Treatment options for high-grade stage II major salivary gland tumors include the following:</p>

3792<div class="pdq-content-list">

3793<ol id="_103">

3794<li>

3795Localized high-grade salivary gland tumors that are confined to the gland in

3796which they arise may be cured by radical surgery alone.

3797</li>

3798<li>

3799Postoperative radiation therapy may improve local control and increase

3800survival rates for patients with high-grade tumors, positive surgical

3801margins, or perineural invasion.[<a href="#cit/section_6.7">

38027</a>

3803][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

3804Level of evidence C2</a>

3805]; [<a href="#cit/section_6.8">

38068</a>

3807-<a href="#cit/section_6.10">

380810</a>

3809]

3810</li>

3811<li>

3812Fast neutron-beam radiation therapy or accelerated hyperfractionated photon-beam

3813schedules reportedly are more effective than conventional x-ray

3814therapy in the treatment of patients with inoperable, unresectable, or recurrent malignant

3815salivary gland tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_6.11">

381611</a>

3817-<a href="#cit/section_6.14">

381814</a>

3819]</li>

3820<li>

3821Chemotherapy (under clinical evaluation).[<a href="#cit/section_6.15">

382215</a>

3823,<a href="#cit/section_6.16">

382416</a>

3825]</li>

3826</ol>

3827</div>

3828<p id="_437" tabindex="-1">

3829Clinical trials exploring ways to improve local control with radiation therapy

3830and/or radiosensitizers are appropriate. </p>

3831<p id="_447" tabindex="-1">

3832High-grade stage II salivary gland tumors that are confined to the gland in

3833which they arise may be cured by surgery alone, although adjuvant radiation

3834therapy may be used, especially if positive margins are present. Primary

3835radiation therapy may be given for tumors that are inoperable, unresectable, or

3836recurrent. Fast neutron-beam radiation therapy has been shown to improve

3837disease-free survival and overall survival in this clinical situation.[<a href="#cit/section_6.11">

383811</a>

3839,<a href="#cit/section_6.13">

384013</a>

3841,<a href="#cit/section_6.14">

384214</a>

3843]</p>

3844</section>

Cancer 50 (11): 2261-4, 1982.&#160;<a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=6754060&amp;dopt=Abstract" title="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&amp;db=PubMed&amp;list_uids=6754060&amp;dopt=Abstract">

3918[PUBMED Abstract]</a>

3919</li>

3920</ol>

3921</div>
