3927 <section id="_73">

3928

3929 <h2>

3930Treatment of Stage III Major Salivary Gland Cancer</h2>

3931

3932 <div id="_section_73" class="pdq-sections">

3933<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

3934<h6>

3935In This Section</h6>

3936<ul>

3937<li>

3938<a href="#_77_toc">

3939Treatment Options for Low-Grade Stage III Major Salivary Gland Tumors</a>

3940</li>

3941<li>

3942<a href="#_83_toc">

3943Treatment Options for High-Grade Stage III Major Salivary Gland Tumors</a>

3944</li>

3945<li>

3946<a href="#_TrialSearch_73_sid_7_toc">

3947Current Clinical Trials</a>

3948</li>

3949</ul>

3950</nav>

3951<section id="_77">

3952<h3 id="_77_toc">

3953Treatment Options for Low-Grade Stage III Major Salivary Gland Tumors</h3>

3954<p id="_448" tabindex="-1">

3955Treatment options for low-grade stage III major salivary gland tumors include the following:</p>

3956<div class="pdq-content-list">

3957<ol id="_105">

3958<li>

3959Surgery alone or with postoperative radiation therapy, if indicated, is appropriate.

3960</li>

3961<li>

3962Chemotherapy should be considered in special circumstances, such as when radiation

3963or surgery is refused or when tumors are recurrent or nonresponsive.</li>

3964<li>

3965Fast neutron-beam radiation therapy (under clinical evaluation). Data in which fast neutron-beam radiation therapy has been used have indicated superior results when

3966compared with conventional radiation therapy using x-rays.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

39671</a>

3968,<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

39692</a>

3970]</li>

3971<li>

3972Chemotherapy (under clinical evaluation).[<a href="#cit/section_7.3">

39733</a>

3974,<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

39754</a>

3976]</li>

3977</ol>

3978</div>

3979<p id="_449" tabindex="-1">

3980Patients with low-grade stage III tumors of the salivary gland may be cured with surgery

3981alone.[<a href="#cit/section_7.5">

39825</a>

3983-<a href="#cit/section_7.7">

39847</a>

3985] Radiation therapy as primary treatment is not often required but

3986may be used for tumors for which resection involves a significant cosmetic or

3987functional deficit, or as an adjuvant to surgery when positive margins are

3988present.[<a href="#cit/section_7.8">

39898</a>

3990] Patients with low-grade tumors that have spread to lymph nodes may be cured with

3991resection of the primary tumor and the involved lymph nodes, with or without

3992radiation therapy. Neutron-beam therapy is effective in the treatment of

3993patients with tumors that have spread to local lymph nodes.

3994</p>

3995</section>

3996<section id="_83">

3997<h3 id="_83_toc">

3998Treatment Options for High-Grade Stage III Major Salivary Gland Tumors</h3>

3999<p id="_450" tabindex="-1">

4000Treatment options for high-grade stage III major salivary gland tumors include the following:</p>

4001<div class="pdq-content-list">

4002<ol id="_107">

4003<li>

4004Patients with localized high-grade salivary gland tumors that are confined to the gland in

4005which they arise may be cured by radical surgery alone.[<a href="#cit/section_7.9">

40069</a>

4007,<a href="#cit/section_7.10">

400810</a>

4009]

4010</li>

4011<li>

4012Postoperative radiation therapy may improve local control and increase

4013survival rates for patients with high-grade tumors, positive surgical

4014margins, or perineural invasion.[<a href="#cit/section_7.11">

401511</a>

4016][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810037&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

4017Level of evidence C2</a>

4018]; [<a href="#cit/section_7.12">

401912</a>

4020-<a href="#cit/section_7.14">

402114</a>

4022]

4023</li>

4024<li>

4025Fast neutron-beam radiation therapy or accelerated hyperfractionated photon-beam

4026schedules have been reported to be more effective than conventional x-ray

4027therapy in the treatment of patients with inoperable, unresectable, or recurrent malignant

4028salivary gland tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

40291</a>

4030,<a href="#cit/section_7.15">

403115</a>

4032-<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

403317</a>

4034]

4035</li>

4036<li>

4037Radiation therapy, radiosensitizers, and chemotherapy (under clinical evaluation). Clinical trials are exploring ways to improve local control with these modalities.[<a href="#cit/section_7.2">

40382</a>

4039-<a href="#cit/section_7.4">

40404</a>

4041,<a href="#cit/section_7.18">

404218</a>

4043,<a href="#cit/section_7.19">

404419</a>

4045]</li>

4046</ol>

4047</div>

4048<p id="_451" tabindex="-1">

4049Patients with high-grade stage III salivary gland tumors that are confined to the gland in

4050which they arise may be cured by surgery alone, although adjuvant postoperative

4051radiation therapy may be used, especially if positive margins are present.

4052Primary conventional x-ray radiation therapy may provide palliation for patients with unresectable tumors. Fast neutron beams, however, have been reported to

4053improve disease-free survival and overall survival in this clinical situation.[<a href="#cit/section_7.1">

40541</a>

4055,<a href="#cit/section_7.16">

405616</a>

4057,<a href="#cit/section_7.17">

405817</a>

4059] Patients with tumors that have spread to regional lymph nodes should have a regional

4060lymphadenectomy as part of the initial surgical procedure. Adjuvant radiation

4061therapy for these tumors may reduce the local recurrence rate.

4062</p>

4063</section>

4069advanced clinical trial search</a>

4070 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

4071General information</a>

4072 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

4158 <section id="_90">

4159

4160 <h2>

4161Treatment of Stage IV Major Salivary Gland Cancer</h2>

4162

4163 <div id="_section_90" class="pdq-sections">

4164<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4165<h6>

4166In This Section</h6>

4167<ul>

4168<li>

4169<a href="#_452_toc">

4170Treatment Options for Stage IV Major Salivary Gland Tumors</a>

4171</li>

4172</ul>

4173</nav>

4174<section id="_452">

4175<h3 id="_452_toc">

4176Treatment Options for Stage IV Major Salivary Gland Tumors</h3>

4177<p id="_453" tabindex="-1">

4178Standard therapy for patients with tumors that have spread to distant sites is not curative.</p>

4179<p id="_454" tabindex="-1">

4180Treatment options for high-grade stage IV major salivary gland tumors include the following:</p>

4181<div class="pdq-content-list">

4182<ol id="_455">

4183<li>

4184Fast neutron-beam radiation therapy or accelerated hyperfractionated photon-beam

4185schedules have been reported to be more effective than conventional x-ray

4186therapy in the treatment of patients with inoperable, unresectable, or recurrent malignant

4187salivary gland tumors.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

41881</a>

4189-<a href="#cit/section_8.5">

41905</a>

4191]</li>

4192<li>

4193Aggressive combinations of chemotherapy and radiation (under clinical evaluation).</li>

4194</ol>

4195</div>

4196<p id="_456" tabindex="-1">

4197Patients with stage IV salivary gland cancer and patients with any metastatic lesions should consider enrollment in clinical trials. Their cancer

4198may be responsive to aggressive combinations of chemotherapy and radiation.

4199Patients with any metastatic lesions could consider clinical trials. Chemotherapy

4200using doxorubicin, cisplatin, cyclophosphamide, and fluorouracil as single

4201agents or in various combinations is associated with modest response rates.[<a href="#cit/section_8.6">

42026</a>

4203-<a href="#cit/section_8.14">

420414</a>

4205]</p>

4206</section>

4271

4272

4273 <section id="_96">

4274

4275 <h2>

4276Treatment of Recurrent Major Salivary Gland Cancer</h2>

4277

4278 <div id="_section_96" class="pdq-sections">

4279<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

4280<h6>

4281In This Section</h6>

4282<ul>

4283<li>

4284<a href="#_TrialSearch_96_sid_9_toc">

4285Current Clinical Trials</a>

4286</li>

4287</ul>

4288</nav>

4289<p id="_97" tabindex="-1">

4290The prognosis for any treated cancer patient with progressing or relapsing

4291disease is poor, regardless of cell type or stage. Selecting further treatment

4292depends on many factors, including the specific cancer, prior treatment, site

4293of recurrence, and individual patient considerations. Fast neutron-beam radiation therapy is superior to conventional radiation

4294therapy using x-rays and may be curative in selected patients with recurrent

4295disease.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

42961</a>

4297]

4298</p>

4299<p id="_217" tabindex="-1">

4300Patients with inoperable,

4301unresectable, or recurrent malignant salivary gland tumors treated with fast neutron-beam radiation therapy have better disease-free survival and overall survival than patients treated with conventional

4302x-ray radiation therapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.2">

43032</a>

4304-<a href="#cit/section_9.5">

43055</a>

4306] Clinical trials are appropriate and should be

4307considered when possible.

4308 </p>

4309<section id="_TrialSearch_96_sid_9">

4310<h3 id="_TrialSearch_96_sid_9_toc">

4311Current Clinical Trials</h3>

4312<p id="_TrialSearch_96_22" tabindex="-1">

4313Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

4314advanced clinical trial search</a>

4315 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

4316General information</a>

4317 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

4318</section>

4361PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

4362, which is

4363editorially independent of NCI. The summary reflects an independent review of

4378 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

4379

4380 <h2>

4381About This PDQ Summary</h2>

4382

4383 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

4384<section id="_AboutThis_2">

4385<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

4386Purpose of This Summary</h3>

4387<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

4388This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of adult salivary gland cancer. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

4389</section>

4390<section id="_AboutThis_4">

4391<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

4392Reviewers and Updates</h3>

4393<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

4394This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/adult-treatment">

4395PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board</a>

4396, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

4397<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

4398 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

4399<div class="pdq-content-list">

4400<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

4401<li>

4402be discussed at a meeting,</li>

4403<li>

4404be cited with text, or</li>

4405<li>

4406replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

4407</ul>

4408</div>

4409<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

4410Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

4411<p id="" tabindex="-1">

4412The lead reviewers for Salivary Gland Cancer Treatment are:</p>

4413<div class="pdq-content-list">

4414<ul id="">

4415<li>

4416Andrea Bonetti, MD (Azienda ULSS 9 of the Veneto Region)</li>

4417<li>

4418Ann W. Gramza, MD (Georgetown Lombardi Comprehensive Cancer Center)</li>

4419<li>

4420Monaliben Patel, MD (Advocate Christ Medical Center)</li>

4421<li>

4422Minh Tam Truong, MD (Boston University Medical Center)</li>

4423</ul>

4424</div>

4425<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

4426Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

4427Email Us</a>

4428. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

4429</section>

4430<section id="_AboutThis_10">

4431<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

4432Levels of Evidence</h3>

4433<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

4434Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Adult Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

4435formal evidence ranking system</a>

4436 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

4437</section>

4438<section id="_AboutThis_12">

4439<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

4440Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

4441<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

4442PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

4443<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

4444The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

4445<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

4446PDQ&#174; Adult Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Salivary Gland Cancer Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq">

4447https://www.cancer.gov/types/head-and-neck/hp/adult/salivary-gland-treatment-pdq</a>

4458Disclaimer</h3>

More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

4461Managing Cancer Care</a>

4462 page.</p>
